Q: When is the "Invisible Fight: Chronic Illness Support Group"?
A: October 15, 2024 at 4 - 5 p.m. Weekly (to Dec 17).
Q: Can you give me some information about "Invisible Fight: Chronic Illness Support Group"?
A: Living with a chronic illness/medical condition can be an isolating experience. This support group is an opportunity for students who experience chronic conditions (i.e. asthma, diabetes, autoimmune diseases, cancer, and others) to gather in community for support and validation.

Q: When is the "Diwali"?
A: The event will be open on November 1, 2024 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Diwali"?
A:   The festival of lights, which typically lasts five days and symbolizes the spiritual “victory of light over darkness, good over evil and knowledge over ignorance.” The Hindu, Sikh and Jain traditions all honor Diwali, each tradition with its own understanding of the meaning.    Carnegie Mellon University intentionally fosters a community where all voices and views are heard and respected, which includes religious backgrounds and spiritual beliefs.

Q: Can you give me some information about "Imbolc or St. Brigid’s Day"?

Q: Is there a specific location to enter for the "Here to Stay: Celebrating 40 Years at the Architecture Archives"?
A: Yes, it is held at Hunt Library, Fourth Floor.
Q: When is the "Here to Stay: Celebrating 40 Years at the Architecture Archives"?
A: The event will be open on May 23 - June 1, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Here to Stay: Celebrating 40 Years at the Architecture Archives"?
A: This University Libraries’ exhibition celebrates the 40th anniversary of the Architecture Archives, which was founded to create, conserve and promote the rich history of Pittsburgh’s buildings and tell part of the story of this dynamic city.

Q: Can you give me some information about "Ramadan"?
A: Ramadan is one of the most important Muslim seasons, commemorating the revelation of the Qur’an to the Prophet Mohamed. Many Muslims fast from both food and drink between sunrise and sunset, honor halal food guidelines when they break the fast with the iftar meal, and spend more time reading the Qu’ran and praying, either alone or at a mosque.

Q: Can you give me some information about "Great Lent"?

Q: When is the "Ash Wednesday"?
A: The event will be open on March 5, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Ash Wednesday"?
A: Some Western Christians honor Ash Wednesday as the first day of Lent, which is the period of 40 days before Easter in which they may sacrifice ordinary pleasures to reflect on Christ’s sacrifice. On this day, there are special church services and participants may receive a cross of ashes marked on their foreheads. Christians may abstain from meat on this day.

A: Yes, it is held at Hunt Library, Fourth Floor.
Q: When is the "Here to Stay: Celebrating 40 Years at the Architecture Archives"?
A: The event will be open on May 23 - June 1, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Here to Stay: Celebrating 40 Years at the Architecture Archives"?
A: This University Libraries’ exhibition celebrates the 40th anniversary of the Architecture Archives, which was founded to create, conserve and promote the rich history of Pittsburgh’s buildings and tell part of the story of this dynamic city.
Q: When is the "Lent / Great Lent"?
A: The event will be open on March 6 - April 12, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Lent / Great Lent"?
A: This year, the season of Lent, which is honored by some Western Christians, and Great Lent of Eastern Orthodoxy, are overlapping. Observations include forms of fasting and prayer.
Q: When is the "Ramadan"?
A: The event will be open on Feb. 28 - March 29, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Ramadan"?
A: Ramadan is one of the most important Muslim seasons, commemorating the revelation of the Qur’an to the Prophet Mohamed. Many Muslims fast from both food and drink between sunrise and sunset, honor halal food guidelines when they break the fast with the iftar meal, and spend more time reading the Qu’ran and praying, either alone or at a mosque.

Q: When is the "Holi"?
A: The event will be open on March 14, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Holi"?
A: On March 14, Hindus celebrate Holi, which is known as the Festival of Colors, Festival of Spring, and the Festival of Love. It marks the arrival of spring, the divine love of Radha Krishna, and the victory of good over evil with a celebration of color and maybe attendance at their temple. This year, CMU will hold its own celebration of Holi on April 6, the Sunday of Carnival weekend.

Q: When is the "Naw Rúz"?
A: The event will be open on March 19 - 20, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Naw Rúz"?
A: Rooted in Zoroastrianism, March 20 or 21 is the New Year celebration for Bahá’ís and Iranians. For some, it marks the end of 19 days of fasting. Naw Rúz celebrations include a feast with traditional and symbolic foods and giving gifts.
Q: When is the "Ramadan"?

Q: Can you give me some information about "Ramadan"?
A: Ramadan is one of the most important Muslim seasons, commemorating the revelation of the Qur’an to the Prophet Mohamed. Many Muslims fast from both food and drink between sunrise and sunset, honor halal food guidelines when they break the fast with the iftar meal, and spend more time reading the Qu’ran and praying, either alone or at a mosque.

Q: Can you give me some information about "Eid al-Fitr"?
A: On Eid al-Fitr, Muslims gather to celebrate the festival of breaking the Ramadan fast by praying to Allah, sharing presents, and feasting with friends and relatives. The celebration begins at sundown, the evening before the appointed day. The March 30 or 31 date is approximate, with the final date determined by the sight of the moon.

Q: Where can I see the "Here to Stay: Celebrating 40 Years at the Architecture Archives"?
A: Hunt Library, Fourth Floor.

A: Yes, it is held at Hunt Library, Fourth Floor.
Q: When is the "Here to Stay: Celebrating 40 Years at the Architecture Archives"?
A: The event will be open on May 23 - June 1, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Here to Stay: Celebrating 40 Years at the Architecture Archives"?
A: This University Libraries’ exhibition celebrates the 40th anniversary of the Architecture Archives, which was founded to create, conserve and promote the rich history of Pittsburgh’s buildings and tell part of the story of this dynamic city.

A: This year, the season of Lent, which is honored by some Western Christians, and Great Lent of Eastern Orthodoxy, are overlapping. Observations include forms of fasting and prayer.

Q: When is the "Ram Navami"?
A: The event will be open on April 6, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Ram Navami"?
A: Ram Navami, which occurs on April 5, celebrates the birth of Lord Rama. To honor this day, Hindus clean and decorate their houses with fruits and flowers. They put an image of Rama as a baby in a cradle, and at midday, they remove the cover of the cradle and feed a special food (called Prasad) to him.

Q: When is the "Mahavir Jayanti"?
A: The event will be open on April 10, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Mahavir Jayanti"?
A: On April 10, the Jain Community celebrates Mahavir Jayanti, the birthday of Lord Mahavir, who taught non-violence, peace, and harmony. The day is honored with special decorations depicting Lord Mahavir, charitable acts, and prayers in Jain temples.

Q: When is the "Day of Silence"?
A: The event will be open on April 11, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Day of Silence"?
A: The Day of Silence is a student-led national event to highlight the silencing and erasure of LGBTQ+ people. Participants take a vow of silence for the day, which ends with a Breaking the Silence rally to speak about their experiences and raise awareness of ways that schools and communities can be more inclusive.

Q: When is the "Passover"?
A: The event will be open on April 12 - 20, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Passover"?
A: Passover (or Pesach, in Hebrew) is celebrated in remembrance of the Israelites being freed from slavery in ancient Egypt and lasts from April 12-20 this year. Beginning at sundown the night before, rituals include telling the story, fasting from leavened bread, and participating in family seder meals. Many Jews keep kosher food restrictions during this festival and attend additional religious services.

Q: When is the "Holy Week or Passion Week"?
A: The event will be open on April 13 - 19, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Holy Week or Passion Week"?
A: Beginning with Palm Sunday on April 13, Eastern Orthodox Christians and some Western Christians commemorate the last week before Pascha or Easter Day with Passion Week or Holy Week. There are special worship services and observances such as prayer, fasting, and confession on multiple days, depending on the specific denomination.

Q: Can you give me some information about "Theravada New Year"?
A: This year on April 13, Theravada Buddhists celebrate the new year with traditions that focus on water, understanding that it cleanses the negativity of the previous year. It’s also a time for giving to charity as a way of growing in enlightenment.

Q: When is the "Vaisakhi"?
A: The event will be open on April 14, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Vaisakhi"?
A: Vaisakhi – which is also called Lohri, Pongal, Sankranthi, Gudi Padwa, and Varsh Pratipada – marks the birth of the Sikh faith, which occurred during the traditional harvest festival in Punjab. Sikh and Hindu celebrations of this festival day (April 14) may include visits to Gurdwaras, special decorations, and singing hymns.

Q: When is the "Holy Week or Passion Week"?
A: The event will be open on April 13 - 19, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Holy Week or Passion Week"?
A: Beginning with Palm Sunday on April 13, Eastern Orthodox Christians and some Western Christians commemorate the last week before Pascha or Easter Day with Passion Week or Holy Week. There are special worship services and observances such as prayer, fasting, and confession on multiple days, depending on the specific denomination.
Q: When is the "National Arab American Heritage Month"?
A: The event will be open on April 1 - 30, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "National Arab American Heritage Month"?
A: National Arab American Heritage Month - During Arab American Heritage Month, the US celebrates the cultural and leadership contributions of Arab Americans.
Q: When is the "Passover"?
A: The event will be open on April 12 - 20, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Passover"?
A: Passover (or Pesach, in Hebrew) is celebrated in remembrance of the Israelites being freed from slavery in ancient Egypt and lasts from April 12-20 this year. Beginning at sundown the night before, rituals include telling the story, fasting from leavened bread, and participating in family seder meals. Many Jews keep kosher food restrictions during this festival and attend additional religious services.

Q: Can you give me some information about "Ridván"?
A: Ridván is a 12-day festival which translates from Arabic to mean “paradise.” Though it lasts from April 20 - May 2, Baha’is observe the three holy days of the festival— the first, ninth, and twelfth—with community gatherings and rest from work.

Q: When is the "Ridván"?
A: The event will be open on April 20 - May 2, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Ridván"?
A: Ridván is a 12-day festival which translates from Arabic to mean “paradise.” Though it lasts from April 20 - May 2, Baha’is observe the three holy days of the festival— the first, ninth, and twelfth—with community gatherings and rest from work.

Q: When is the "Beltane"?
A: The event will be open on May 1, 2025 all day.
Q: Can you give me some information about "Beltane"?
A: Beltane, which means “bright fire” in Gaelic, is celebrated on May 1 and represents the beginning of summer in early Celtic traditions. Current Wiccan and Pagan practices honor Beltane by holding ceremonies that honor fertility, creativity, and rebirth, and fires are lit.
